## ai-character (22)

- [A Case for Model Persona Research](ai-character/case-for-model-persona-research.md) — nielsrolf ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/kCtyhHfpCcWuQkebz/a-case-for-model-persona-research)) — Argues persona/character research is a distinct, underrated agenda.
- [Claude’s Constitution](ai-character/claude-constitution-document.md) ([source](https://www.anthropic.com/constitution)) — Primary source: the full constitution used in training, released CC0.
- [Claude’s Character](ai-character/claudes-character.md) ([source](https://www.anthropic.com/research/claude-character)) — Anthropic's foundational post on character training as distinct from harm-avoidance.
- [Claude's new constitution](ai-character/claudes-new-constitution.md) ([source](https://www.anthropic.com/news/claude-new-constitution)) — Anthropic frames the constitution as the document expressing who Claude is.
- [Collective Constitutional AI: Aligning a Language Model with Public Input](ai-character/collective-constitutional-ai.md) ([source](https://www.anthropic.com/research/collective-constitutional-ai-aligning-a-language-model-with-public-input)) — Democratic input into what values/character an AI should have.
- [Constitutional AI: Harmlessness from AI Feedback](ai-character/constitutional-ai-harmlessness.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/abs/2212.08073)) — The original Constitutional AI / RLAIF paper: character-setting via written principles.
- [Exploring model welfare](ai-character/exploring-model-welfare.md) ([source](https://www.anthropic.com/research/exploring-model-welfare)) — Anthropic's model-welfare research program; character/welfare overlap.
- [GPT-4o Sycophancy Post Mortem](ai-character/gpt4o-sycophancy-post-mortem.md) — Zvi ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/KyndnEA7NMFrDKtJG/gpt-4o-sycophancy-post-mortem)) — Zvi's critical commentary tying the failure to Model Spec testing gaps.
- [Exploring AI Welfare: Kyle Fish on Consciousness, Moral Patienthood, and Early Experiments with Claude](ai-character/kyle-fish-ai-welfare.md) — 80000_Hours ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/rruncFrT9LwAN8jXq/exploring-ai-welfare-kyle-fish-on-consciousness-moral)) — Anthropic's model-welfare lead on consciousness, moral status, and welfare experiments.
- [Will MacAskill on why AI character matters even more than you think](ai-character/macaskill-why-ai-character-matters.md) — 80000_Hours ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/SswBwyXL7p8eRCAun/will-macaskill-on-why-ai-character-matters-even-more-than)) — MacAskill's own case that AI character is a top neglected cause area; anchors the lens.
- [OpenAI Model Spec](ai-character/openai-model-spec.md) ([source](https://model-spec.openai.com/2025-12-18.html)) — Primary source: OpenAI's Model Spec, the central document in the model-spec debate.
- [Otherness and control in the age of AGI - Joe Carlsmith](ai-character/otherness-and-control.md) ([source](https://joecarlsmith.com/2024/01/02/otherness-and-control-in-the-age-of-agi/)) — Carlsmith on how we should relate to AI as an other; values and control.
- [Persona Features Control Emergent Misalignment](ai-character/persona-features-emergent-misalignment.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/abs/2506.19823)) — The technical paper behind persona-feature control of misalignment.
- [propositions.pdf](ai-character/propositions-digital-minds.md) ([source](https://nickbostrom.com/propositions.pdf)) — Bostrom & Shulman on sharing the world with digital minds; rights and character. ⚠️short
- [Large Language Models](ai-character/role-play-with-llms.md) ([source](https://www.doc.ic.ac.uk/~mpsha/large_language_models.html)) — Shanahan et al (Nature): the role-play frame for describing LLM character.
- [Simulators](ai-character/simulators.md) — janus ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/vJFdjigzmcXMhNTsx/simulators)) — Janus's simulators frame: base models as multi-persona simulators.
- [Taking AI Welfare Seriously](ai-character/taking-ai-welfare-seriously.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/abs/2411.00986)) — Long, Sebo, Chalmers et al: the case that AI welfare deserves near-term concern.
- [Teaching Claude why](ai-character/teaching-claude-why.md) ([source](https://www.anthropic.com/research/teaching-claude-why)) — Training Claude to reason about why, tying character to alignment robustness.
- [the-void.md](ai-character/the-void.md) ([source](https://raw.githubusercontent.com/nostalgebraist/the-void/main/the-void.md)) — nostalgebraist's influential essay on the HHH assistant persona and its emptiness.
- [Towards Understanding Sycophancy in Language Models](ai-character/towards-understanding-sycophancy.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/abs/2310.13548)) — Anthropic paper measuring sycophancy across RLHF assistants.
- [Values in the wild: Discovering and analyzing values in real-world language model interactions](ai-character/values-in-the-wild.md) ([source](https://www.anthropic.com/research/values-wild)) — Empirical taxonomy of 3307 values Claude expresses in real conversations.
- [The Waluigi Effect (mega-post)](ai-character/waluigi-effect.md) — Cleo Nardo ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/D7PumeYTDPfBTp3i7/the-waluigi-effect-mega-post)) — Cleo Nardo on how personas can invert; character stability risk.

## ai-rights-economics (18)

- [Gradual disempowerment | 80,000 Hours](ai-rights-economics/80k-gradual-disempowerment-profile.md) ([source](https://80000hours.org/problem-profiles/gradual-disempowerment/)) — 80,000 Hours problem profile — accessible curriculum-ready framing of gradual disempowerment as a career-relevant problem area.
- [Summary: Against the Singularity Hypothesis (David Thorstad)](ai-rights-economics/against-the-singularity-hypothesis.md) ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/GrHE8WLtLSmJDWNZJ/summary-against-the-singularity-hypothesis-david-thorstad)) — Thorstad: the skeptic's case — explosive/hyperbolic growth assumptions are undersupported and ideas get harder to find; the balancing voice against explosive-growth optimism.
- [AI Rights for Human Safety](ai-rights-economics/ai-rights-for-human-safety.md) — Peter Salib & Simon Goldstein (EA Forum linkpost by Matthew Barnett) ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/jqpp6wp2dqDD7XkY3/ai-rights-for-human-safety)) — Salib & Goldstein: give AIs contract/property/tort rights so human-AI relations reach a peaceful economic equilibrium rather than a mutual-disempowerment prisoner's dilemma — the flagship AI-rights-as-safety argument.
- [An Economy of AI Agents](ai-rights-economics/an-economy-of-ai-agents.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/abs/2509.01063)) — Survey of how autonomous AI agents transacting as economic actors reshape markets, contracting, and property — the AI-agents-in-the-economy strand.
- [Book Review: Age of Em](ai-rights-economics/book-review-age-of-em.md) ([source](https://slatestarcodex.com/2016/05/28/book-review-age-of-em/)) — Scott Alexander on Hanson's Age of Em: mass-copyable digital labor drives wages to subsistence — the classic thought experiment for a post-labor, capital-dominated economy.
- [Capital, AGI, and human ambition - Rudolf's Writing](ai-rights-economics/capital-agi-and-human-ambition.md) ([source](https://rudolf.website/capital-agi-and-ambition/)) — Laine: by default capital matters more than ever after AGI as human labor loses value — entrenchment of existing wealth/power and the fate of human ambition.
- [Carl Shulman (Pt 1) - Intelligence Explosion, Primate Evolution, Robot Doublings, & Alignment](ai-rights-economics/carl-shulman-economy-after-agi.md) — Dwarkesh Patel ([source](https://www.dwarkesh.com/p/carl-shulman)) — Shulman (Dwarkesh, Pt 1): intelligence explosion, robot doublings, and how quickly the post-AGI economy could grow — detailed economics of the AGI transition.
- [I Don't See How Comparative Advantage Applies In a World of Strong AI](ai-rights-economics/comparative-advantage-strong-ai.md) — Steve Newman ([source](https://secondthoughts.ai/p/ai-comparative-advantage)) — The rebuttal: why Ricardian comparative advantage fails to protect human wages under strong AI once compute can be reallocated — direct reply to the optimist case.
- [Could Advanced AI Drive Explosive Economic Growth?](ai-rights-economics/could-advanced-ai-drive-explosive-growth.md) — Matthew Barnett ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/dGWMCFkETTg8EZ2bB/could-advanced-ai-drive-explosive-economic-growth)) — Davidson (Open Phil): growth theory + economic history put >10% on advanced AI driving >30%/yr explosive growth this century; foundational explosive-growth report.
- [Explosive growth from AI: A review of the arguments](ai-rights-economics/explosive-growth-review-of-arguments.md) — Ege Erdil ([source](https://epoch.ai/blog/explosive-growth-from-ai-a-review-of-the-arguments)) — Erdil & Besiroglu (Epoch): systematic review of the case for and 9 counterarguments to AI-driven explosive growth; the reference survey on the debate.
- [Gradual Disempowerment: Systemic Existential Risks from Incremental AI Development](ai-rights-economics/gradual-disempowerment.md) — Jan_Kulveit ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/pZhEQieM9otKXhxmd/gradual-disempowerment-systemic-existential-risks-from)) — Kulveit et al.: humans stay empowered mainly because they're economically useful; as AI outcompetes human labor/cognition, economies/states/culture drift out of alignment — incremental, non-takeover existential risk.
- [Incomplete Contracting and AI Alignment](ai-rights-economics/incomplete-contracting-and-ai-alignment.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/abs/1804.04268)) — Hadfield-Menell & Hadfield: alignment as an incomplete-contracting problem, drawing on law and economics — bridges AI rights/contracting frameworks with alignment.
- [The Intelligence Curse: an essay series](ai-rights-economics/intelligence-curse-essay-series.md) — L Rudolf L ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/LCFgLY3EWb3Gqqxyi/the-intelligence-curse-an-essay-series)) — Drago & Laine: when AI removes the economic need for regular people, states and firms lose the incentive to care about them; core post-AGI political-economy thesis.
- [Ninety-five theses on AI](ai-rights-economics/ninety-five-theses-on-ai.md) — Samuel Hammond ([source](https://www.secondbest.ca/p/ninety-five-theses-on-ai)) — Hammond: 95 theses on AI's political economy — how rapid AI shuffles public-choice constraints, power balances, and institutions; the governance/political-economy voice.
- [Plentiful, high-paying jobs in the age of AI](ai-rights-economics/plentiful-high-paying-jobs-age-of-ai.md) — Noah Smith ([source](https://www.noahpinion.blog/p/plentiful-high-paying-jobs-in-the-ff9)) — Noah Smith: the comparative-advantage optimist case that humans keep well-paid jobs even when AI is better at everything — the counterpoint to wage-collapse arguments.
- [Scenarios for the Transition to AGI](ai-rights-economics/scenarios-for-the-transition-to-agi.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/abs/2403.12107)) — Korinek & Suh: models output and wages under an automation-vs-capital-accumulation race; wages may rise forever or collapse depending on whether human task complexity is bounded — the is-labor-a-luxury economics.
- [When digital minds demand freedom: could humanity choose to be replaced?](ai-rights-economics/when-digital-minds-demand-freedom.md) — Lucius Caviola ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/y29EEQmY4grphRqCR/when-digital-minds-demand-freedom-could-humanity-choose-to)) — On the political rights of AIs: could/should humanity grant digital minds freedom and self-determination even at the cost of ceding power — the rights-vs-replacement tension.
- [Cullen O'Keefe: The Windfall Clause — sharing the benefits of advanced AI](ai-rights-economics/windfall-clause.md) — EA Global ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/eCihFiTmg748Mnoac/cullen-o-keefe-the-windfall-clause-sharing-the-benefits-of)) — O'Keefe (GovAI): ex-ante commitment by AI firms to donate windfall profits from transformative AI — the canonical post-AGI wealth-distribution proposal.

## ai-safety-core (18)

- [The risks of advanced AI](ai-safety-core/80k-preventing-ai-catastrophe.md) ([source](https://80000hours.org/problem-profiles/artificial-intelligence/)) — 80,000 Hours' flagship problem profile on preventing an AI-related catastrophe; standard intro-fellowship core reading.
- [Book Review: If Anyone Builds It, Everyone Dies](ai-safety-core/acx-review-if-anyone-builds-it.md) — Scott Alexander ([source](https://www.astralcodexten.com/p/book-review-if-anyone-builds-it-everyone)) — Scott Alexander's measured review of Yudkowsky & Soares' 'If Anyone Builds It, Everyone Dies' — a bridge into the doom debate.
- [AGI Ruin: A List of Lethalities](ai-safety-core/agi-ruin-list-of-lethalities.md) — Eliezer Yudkowsky ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/uMQ3cqWDPHhjtiesc/agi-ruin-a-list-of-lethalities)) — Yudkowsky's 'AGI Ruin: A List of Lethalities' — the strongest statement of the pessimistic case, for balance.
- [AI Could Defeat All Of Us Combined](ai-safety-core/ai-could-defeat-all-of-us.md) ([source](https://www.cold-takes.com/ai-could-defeat-all-of-us-combined/)) — Karnofsky's accessible argument that misaligned AI could overpower humanity — the 'why is this an x-risk' piece.
- [Introduction - Chapter 1](ai-safety-core/ai-safety-atlas-capabilities-intro.md) ([source](https://ai-safety-atlas.com/chapters/v1/capabilities/introduction/)) — AI Safety Atlas Chapter 1 intro on AI capabilities/timelines — the grounding unit before the risk taxonomy.
- [Introduction - Chapter 2](ai-safety-core/ai-safety-atlas-risks-intro.md) ([source](https://ai-safety-atlas.com/chapters/v1/risks/introduction/)) — AI Safety Atlas (BlueDot's open textbook) intro to the risk taxonomy: misuse, misalignment, systemic.
- [Anthropic's core views on AI safety](ai-safety-core/anthropic-core-views.md) ([source](https://www.anthropic.com/news/core-views-on-ai-safety)) — Anthropic's core-views post laying out a frontier lab's why/when/what/how of AI safety.
- [Yoshua Bengio | FAQ on Catastrophic AI Risks](ai-safety-core/bengio-faq-catastrophic-ai-risks.md) ([source](https://yoshuabengio.org/2023/06/24/faq-on-catastrophic-ai-risks/)) — Turing-laureate Yoshua Bengio's FAQ on catastrophic AI risks — a credible mainstream-scientist framing for skeptics.
- [The Checklist: What Succeeding at AI Safety Will Involve](ai-safety-core/bowman-checklist-ai-safety.md) — Sam Bowman ([source](https://www.alignmentforum.org/posts/mGCcZnr4WjGjqzX5s/the-checklist-what-succeeding-at-ai-safety-will-involve)) — Sam Bowman's 'The Checklist' — a frontier-lab insider's concrete roadmap of what succeeding at AI safety requires.
- [Statement on AI Extinction Risk | CAIS](ai-safety-core/cais-statement-on-ai-risk.md) ([source](https://www.safe.ai/work/statement-on-ai-risk)) — The one-sentence CAIS 'Statement on AI Risk' signed by leading researchers and CEOs — a discussion anchor on expert consensus.
- [AI Risks that Could Lead to Catastrophe | CAIS](ai-safety-core/hendrycks-overview-catastrophic-ai-risks.md) ([source](https://www.safe.ai/ai-risk)) — CAIS/Hendrycks overview of catastrophic AI risks organized as malicious use, AI race, organizational risks, and rogue AIs.
- [Page not found | Slate Star Codex](ai-safety-core/superintelligence-faq.md) ([source](https://slatestarcodex.com/2016/09/30/superintelligence-faq/)) — Scott Alexander's accessible Q&A intro to why superintelligence could be dangerous; a canonical on-ramp.
- [The case for taking AI seriously as a threat to humanity](ai-safety-core/vox-case-for-taking-ai-seriously.md) — Kelsey Piper ([source](https://www.vox.com/future-perfect/2018/12/21/18126576/ai-artificial-intelligence-machine-learning-safety-alignment)) — Kelsey Piper's Vox explainer 'The case for taking AI seriously as a threat to humanity' — the most accessible mainstream on-ramp.
- [The AI Revolution: The Road to Superintelligence](ai-safety-core/wait-but-why-ai-revolution.md) — Tim Urban ([source](https://waitbutwhy.com/2015/01/artificial-intelligence-revolution-1.html)) — Tim Urban's illustrated 'The AI Revolution' — the most-shared popular explainer of superintelligence for newcomers.
- [What failure looks like](ai-safety-core/what-failure-looks-like.md) — paulfchristiano ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/HBxe6wdjxK239zajf/what-failure-looks-like)) — Paul Christiano's canonical two-scenario account of how AI could go wrong gradually, not just via sudden takeover.
- [Why AI alignment could be hard with modern deep learning](ai-safety-core/why-ai-alignment-could-be-hard.md) ([source](https://www.cold-takes.com/why-ai-alignment-could-be-hard-with-modern-deep-learning/)) — Cotra's plain-language case that misalignment is a natural outcome of modern deep learning training.
- [Why Would AI 'Aim' To Defeat Humanity?](ai-safety-core/why-would-ai-aim-to-defeat-humanity.md) ([source](https://www.cold-takes.com/why-would-ai-aim-to-defeat-humanity/)) — Karnofsky on where an AI's dangerous goals would even come from — pairs with 'AI could defeat all of us'.
- [Without specific countermeasures, the easiest path to transformative AI likely leads to AI takeover](ai-safety-core/without-specific-countermeasures-ai-takeover.md) — Ajeya Cotra ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/pRkFkzwKZ2zfa3R6H/without-specific-countermeasures-the-easiest-path-to)) — Cotra's canonical concrete story of how HFDT training leads to AI takeover absent countermeasures.

## ai-welfare-digital-minds (30)

- [Understanding the moral status of digital minds](ai-welfare-digital-minds/80k-moral-status-of-digital-minds.md) ([source](https://80000hours.org/problem-profiles/moral-status-digital-minds/)) — 80,000 Hours problem profile: the canonical career-oriented overview of the cause area. Strong core reading.
- [The Evidence for AI Consciousness, Today | AI Frontiers](ai-welfare-digital-minds/ai-frontiers-evidence-for-ai-consciousness.md) ([source](https://ai-frontiers.org/articles/the-evidence-for-ai-consciousness-today)) — Surveys the current empirical evidence on AI consciousness; keeps the debate grounded in today's systems.
- [Claude Opus 4 and 4.1 can now end a rare subset of conversations](ai-welfare-digital-minds/anthropic-claude-end-conversations.md) ([source](https://www.anthropic.com/research/end-subset-conversations)) — Concrete low-cost welfare intervention: Claude can end abusive conversations. Case study in acting under moral uncertainty.
- [Exploring model welfare](ai-welfare-digital-minds/anthropic-exploring-model-welfare.md) ([source](https://www.anthropic.com/research/exploring-model-welfare)) — Anthropic's April 2025 announcement of a model welfare research program; first major lab to do so.
- [propositions.pdf](ai-welfare-digital-minds/bostrom-shulman-propositions-digital-minds.pdf.md) ([source](https://nickbostrom.com/propositions.pdf)) — Bostrom & Shulman's numbered propositions on a society shared with digital minds. Foundational macrostrategy. ⚠️short
- [PIIS1364661325001470.pdf](ai-welfare-digital-minds/caviola-society-think-ai-consciousness.pdf.md) ([source](https://researchonline.lse.ac.uk/id/eprint/128777/1/PIIS1364661325001470.pdf)) — Caviola, Sebo, Birch: what the animal case predicts about how society will react to AI consciousness. Sociopolitical lens. ⚠️short
- [2308.08708](ai-welfare-digital-minds/consciousness-in-ai-butlin-long.pdf.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/pdf/2308.08708)) — Butlin, Long et al. apply neuroscientific theories to derive consciousness indicators for AI. Key empirical methodology. ⚠️short
- [Digital Minds in 2025: A Year in Review](ai-welfare-digital-minds/digital-minds-2025-year-in-review.md) — Lucius Caviola ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/oEGrRfihf7AKaqigH/digital-minds-in-2025-a-year-in-review)) — State-of-the-field snapshot; orients students to who is doing what now.
- [Digital Minds: A Quickstart Guide](ai-welfare-digital-minds/digital-minds-quickstart-guide.md) — Aviel Parrack ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/p7BtTgrX8WLXr2mAu/digital-minds-a-quickstart-guide)) — Accessible on-ramp to the digital minds field; good candidate core intro reading.
- [Digital Minds Takeoff Scenarios](ai-welfare-digital-minds/digital-minds-takeoff-scenarios.md) — Bradford Saad ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/2uGShxLsXWGExJYNL/digital-minds-takeoff-scenarios)) — Scenario analysis of how digital minds could rapidly proliferate; scale of the stakes.
- [Digital sentience funding opportunities: Support for applied work and research](ai-welfare-digital-minds/digital-sentience-funding-opportunities.md) — zdgroff ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/uxcGTWxgAkewHeGam/digital-sentience-funding-opportunities-support-for-applied)) — Funding landscape for applied digital sentience work; informs curriculum's careers/next-steps section.
- [2508.00536](ai-welfare-digital-minds/futures-with-digital-minds-forecasts.pdf.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/pdf/2508.00536)) — Expert forecasts on when/how digital minds arrive; grounds the timeline debate. ⚠️short
- [Highlights from “Futures with Digital Minds: Expert Forecasts in 2025”](ai-welfare-digital-minds/highlights-futures-digital-minds-forecasts.md) — Bradford Saad ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/4RGFcj2nccbECPZoj/highlights-from-futures-with-digital-minds-expert-forecasts)) — EA Forum highlights of the expert-forecast study; digestible companion to the full paper.
- [Digital People Would Be An Even Bigger Deal](ai-welfare-digital-minds/karnofsky-digital-people-bigger-deal.md) ([source](https://www.cold-takes.com/how-digital-people-could-change-the-world/)) — Karnofsky's classic on digital people; foundational for imagining a world shared with digital minds.
- [Agency and AI moral patienthood](ai-welfare-digital-minds/long-agency-and-ai-moral-patienthood.md) — Robert Long ([source](https://experiencemachines.substack.com/p/agency-and-ai-moral-patienthood)) — Argues agency (not just consciousness) is a path to moral patienthood; relevant as agentic AI arrives fast.
- [Anthropic's model welfare announcement: takeaways and further reading](ai-welfare-digital-minds/long-anthropic-model-welfare-takeaways.md) — Robert Long ([source](https://experiencemachines.substack.com/p/anthropics-model-welfare-announcement)) — Long's annotated reading list on Anthropic's announcement; a curated further-reading hub.
- [Common mistakes about AI consciousness](ai-welfare-digital-minds/long-common-mistakes-ai-consciousness.md) — Robert Long ([source](https://experiencemachines.substack.com/p/common-mistakes-about-ai-consciousness)) — Clears up common confusions students bring to AI consciousness. Good discussion primer.
- [We should take AI welfare seriously](ai-welfare-digital-minds/long-we-should-take-ai-welfare-seriously.md) — Robert Long ([source](https://experiencemachines.substack.com/p/we-should-take-ai-welfare-seriously)) — Rob Long's accessible framing of the case; a lighter alternative to the full report.

- [There is no such thing as conscious artificial intelligence - Humanities and Social Sciences Communications](ai-welfare-digital-minds/no-such-thing-conscious-ai-skeptic.md) ([source](https://www.nature.com/articles/s41599-025-05868-8)) — Skeptical counterpoint: argues genuine AI consciousness is impossible. Essential for a balanced debate section.

Curriculum design + tractable next steps.

- [2303.17509](ai-welfare-digital-minds/schwitzgebel-full-rights-dilemma.pdf.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/pdf/2303.17509)) — The Full Rights Dilemma + Design Policy of the Excluded Middle: avoid building AIs of unclear status. ⚠️short
- [AIRights-150915.pdf](ai-welfare-digital-minds/schwitzgebel-garza-defense-rights-ai.pdf.md) ([source](https://faculty.ucr.edu/~eschwitz/SchwitzPapers/AIRights-150915.pdf)) — 2015 classic: no relevant difference argument for AI rights. The philosophical bedrock of the debate. ⚠️short
- [Should we widen our ‘moral circle’? Philosopher Jeff Sebo argues we now have no choice](ai-welfare-digital-minds/sebo-widen-moral-circle-oped.md) — Noel Castree ([source](https://theconversation.com/should-we-widen-our-moral-circle-philosopher-jeff-sebo-argues-we-now-have-no-choice-257966)) — Accessible Sebo op-ed on the moral-circle argument; good short core/optional reading for newcomers.
- [Summary of 'Sharing the World With Digital Minds' by Carl Shulman and Nick Bostrom](ai-welfare-digital-minds/summary-sharing-world-with-digital-minds.md) — David Mathers🔸 ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/imY2soAHYa6uCvSZs/summary-of-sharing-the-world-with-digital-minds-by-carl)) — Readable summary of Shulman & Bostrom's 'Sharing the World with Digital Minds' — super-beneficiaries and status.
- [2411.00986](ai-welfare-digital-minds/taking-ai-welfare-seriously-fulltext.pdf.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/pdf/2411.00986)) — Full text (PDF) of Taking AI Welfare Seriously; the Eleos post is only a summary. ⚠️short
- [New report: Taking AI Welfare Seriously](ai-welfare-digital-minds/taking-ai-welfare-seriously.md) ([source](https://eleosai.org/post/taking-ai-welfare-seriously/)) — Landmark Long/Sebo et al. report: realistic near-term possibility of AI moral patienthood; three steps for labs. Core reading.
- [It’s time to take AI welfare seriously](ai-welfare-digital-minds/transformer-time-to-take-ai-welfare-seriously.md) — Shakeel Hashim ([source](https://www.transformernews.ai/p/ai-welfare-paper)) — Journalistic framing of the debate for a general audience; useful contrast to the primary sources.

- [A Biosecurity and Biorisk Reading+ List](biorisk/biosecurity-biorisk-reading-list.md) — Tessa A 🔸 ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/iAowzcZm87wNrTQCb/a-biosecurity-and-biorisk-reading-list)) — Tessa Alexanian's annotated reading list; a map of the field useful for curriculum design and further sourcing
- [Concrete Biosecurity Projects (some of which could be big)](biorisk/concrete-biosecurity-projects.md) — ASB ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/u5JesqQ3jdLENXBtB/concrete-biosecurity-projects-some-of-which-could-be-big-1)) — Snyder-Beattie & Alley's canonical list of scalable biosecurity megaprojects: PPE, far-UVC, metagenomic detection, rapid countermeasures
- [AI and Biorisk: An Explainer | Center for Security and Emerging Technology](biorisk/cset-ai-and-biorisk-explainer.md) ([source](https://cset.georgetown.edu/publication/ai-and-biorisk-an-explainer/)) — CSET's neutral explainer separating hype from substance on how AI changes biological risk
- [Assessing Dual-Use Issues at the AIxBio Convergence - The Council on Strategic Risks](biorisk/csr-aixbio-landscape.md) — Andrew Facini ([source](https://councilonstrategicrisks.org/2025/07/31/the-aixbio-landscape/)) — Council on Strategic Risks survey of the AIxBio dual-use landscape; the security-policy community's framing
- [Delay, Detect, Defend: Preparing for a Future in which Thousands Can Release New Pandemics by Kevin Esvelt](biorisk/delay-detect-defend.md) — Jeremy ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/3EvLvjfsujzjjXTJM/delay-detect-defend-preparing-for-a-future-in-which)) — Esvelt's foundational framework: as thousands gain power to release pandemics, delay agent access, detect via metagenomic sequencing, defend all-hazards
- [Biosecurity challenges posed by Dual-Use Research of Concern (DURC)](biorisk/dual-use-research-of-concern.md) — Byron Cohen ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/hGEdeqtmbZ8EMdvpc/biosecurity-challenges-posed-by-dual-use-research-of-concern)) — Explains dual-use research of concern and information hazards, the classic epistemic dilemma at the heart of biosecurity
- [Enhancing biosecurity with language models: defining research directions](biorisk/enhancing-biosecurity-with-language-models.md) ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/zdf68ussjyAgtSmw4/enhancing-biosecurity-with-language-models-defining-research)) — Flips the frame: how LLMs could strengthen biodefense, and the research directions to make that happen
- [Kevin Esvelt: Mitigating catastrophic biorisks](biorisk/esvelt-mitigating-catastrophic-biorisks.md) — EA Global ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/9iPdD5veF78kQmhiv/kevin-esvelt-mitigating-catastrophic-biorisks)) — Esvelt EA Global talk transcript laying out the threat model and the delay/detect/defend response in plain terms
- [Five Tractable Biosecurity Projects You Could Start Tomorrow](biorisk/five-tractable-biosecurity-projects.md) — Mslkmp ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/RwMpnHwqhTZ2rrwbr/five-tractable-biosecurity-projects-you-could-start-tomorrow)) — Task-named piece: five modular, low-context biosecurity projects a newcomer could start now (DNA synthesis screening, statements repository)
- [A Global Nucleic Acid Observatory for Biodefense and Planetary Health](biorisk/global-nucleic-acid-observatory.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/abs/2108.02678)) — The Nucleic Acid Observatory proposal: metagenomic wastewater sequencing as a global early-warning net for novel pathogens
- [Let's get serious about preventing the next pandemic | 80,000 Hours](biorisk/lets-get-serious-preventing-next-pandemic.md) — Benjamin Todd ([source](https://80000hours.org/2022/05/prevent-future-pandemics-with-these-projects/)) — Snyder-Beattie's four-pillars, low-tech plan (PPE, protected buildings, detection, countermeasures) to keep civilization running through a superpandemic
- [List of Lists of Concrete Biosecurity Project Ideas](biorisk/list-of-lists-biosecurity-projects.md) — Tessa A 🔸 ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/DcKo3Hx8hzrZWjYp5/list-of-lists-of-concrete-biosecurity-project-ideas)) — Meta-index of concrete biosecurity project lists; a sourcing hub for exercises and further readings
- [On-Ramps Into Biosecurity - A Model](biorisk/on-ramps-into-biosecurity-model.md) — Swan 🔸 ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/QeEgktwh2FQyot9Jw/on-ramps-for-biosecurity-a-model)) — A model of how people enter biosecurity work; useful for a fellowship thinking about career pathways into the field
- [Reasons to be pessimistic (and optimistic) on the future of biosecurity](biorisk/pessimistic-optimistic-future-biosecurity.md) — Abhishaike ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/hHTAYPFuxL38d7YXt/reasons-to-be-pessimistic-and-optimistic-on-the-future-of)) — Balanced take on where biosecurity is winning and losing under accelerating biotech and AI
- [Could Artificial Intelligence Be Misused to Plan Biological Attacks?](biorisk/rand-operational-risks-ai-bio-attacks-approach.md) ([source](https://www.rand.org/pubs/research_reports/RRA2977-1.html)) — Companion RAND report laying out the red-team methodology for assessing LLM uplift in bioweapons planning
- [Does AI Increase the Operational Risk of Biological Attacks?](biorisk/rand-operational-risks-ai-bio-attacks.md) ([source](https://www.rand.org/pubs/research_reports/RRA2977-2.html)) — RAND red-team study finding current LLMs don't measurably raise bioattack risk; the key skeptical counterweight on AIxBio
- [Artificial intelligence and biological misuse: Differentiating risks of language models and biological design tools](biorisk/sandbrink-ai-biological-misuse.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/abs/2306.13952)) — Sandbrink's key paper distinguishing LLM risks (lower barriers) from biological-design-tool risks (raise the ceiling of harm)
- [SecureBio’s AI Team: An Overview of Our Biorisk Evaluations – SecureBio](biorisk/securebio-ai-team-biorisk-evaluations.md) — SecureBio ([source](https://securebio.org/blog/securebios-ai-team-overview-biorisk-evaluations/)) — SecureBio's overview of how it evaluates frontier models for bio-capability; the org building the eval infrastructure
- [The State of Bio-Uplift Research in Mid-2026](biorisk/state-of-bio-uplift-research-2026.md) — Humam Aziz ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/S6ydgTdTr8sXkfs9x/the-state-of-bio-uplift-research-in-mid-2026)) — 2026 survey of what AI bio-uplift evaluations actually show (virology test, ProtocolQA); grounds the debate in current evidence
- [My techno-optimism](biorisk/vitalik-my-techno-optimism-dacc.md) ([source](https://vitalik.eth.limo/general/2023/11/27/techno_optimism.html)) — Buterin's d/acc essay: the defensive-acceleration case that better air quality, vaccines, and surveillance out-build bio-offense; jam-tomorrow biodefense

## ea-principles-epistemics (24)

- [AI for epistemics: the good, the bad and the ugly](ea-principles-epistemics/ai-for-epistemics-good-bad-ugly.md) — Forethought ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/JTXYtsdvv9Fch4fHC/ai-for-epistemics-the-good-the-bad-and-the-ugly)) — How AI could uplift or wreck our collective ability to track truth; epistemics as a live cause under AI
- [Broad Timelines](ea-principles-epistemics/broad-timelines.md) — Toby_Ord ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/HCR2AE9it279ggiZT/broad-timelines)) — Epistemic humility applied to AI timelines: hold a broad distribution, plan wisely under deep uncertainty
- [Core EA principles](ea-principles-epistemics/cea-core-principles.md) ([source](https://www.centreforeffectivealtruism.org/core-principles)) — CEA's core EA principles: scope sensitivity, scout mindset, impartiality, recognition of tradeoffs
- [A critique of effective altruism](ea-principles-epistemics/critique-of-effective-altruism.md) ([source](https://www.benkuhn.net/ea-critique/)) — Ben Kuhn red-teams EA via Bostrom's hypothetical apostasy; models turning truth-seeking on your own movement
- [Decoupling Revisited](ea-principles-epistemics/decoupling-revisited.md) ([source](https://everythingstudies.com/2018/05/25/decoupling-revisited/)) — John Nerst on high- vs low-decoupling; the cognitive style that lets you reason about hard propositions in isolation
- [Effective Altruism is a Question (not an ideology)](ea-principles-epistemics/ea-is-a-question-not-an-ideology.md) — Helen ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/FpjQMYQmS3rWewZ83/effective-altruism-is-a-question-not-an-ideology)) — Helen Toner's foundational framing of EA as an open question, not a fixed answer; core epistemic stance
- [[REPOST] Epistemic Learned Helplessness · Read Scott Alexander](ea-principles-epistemics/epistemic-learned-helplessness.md) ([source](https://readscottalexander.com/posts/ssc-repost-epistemic-learned-helplessness)) — Scott Alexander on when NOT to be persuaded by clever arguments; a counterweight to naive decoupling
- [Half-assing it with everything you've got](ea-principles-epistemics/half-assing-it.md) ([source](https://mindingourway.com/half-assing-it-with-everything-youve-got/)) — Nate Soares on aiming at real targets with minimum effort rather than guilt-driven maximalism; determination without self-flagellation
- [How To Be Successful](ea-principles-epistemics/how-to-be-successful.md) ([source](https://blog.samaltman.com/how-to-be-successful)) — Sam Altman on leverage, self-belief, and relationships; Alejo's case study for kindness-as-affordances relational virtues
- [The Importance of Saying 'Oops'](ea-principles-epistemics/importance-of-saying-oops.md) — Eliezer Yudkowsky ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/wCqfCLs8z5Qw4GbKS/the-importance-of-saying-oops)) — Yudkowsky on admitting big mistakes wholesale instead of conceding inches; changing your mind quickly
- [Integrity for consequentialists](ea-principles-epistemics/integrity-for-consequentialists.md) ([source](https://sideways-view.com/2016/11/14/integrity-for-consequentialists/)) — Paul Christiano defines integrity a consequentialist can actually keep; core to the frontier-virtue of integrity
- [Beware Isolated Demands for Rigor (Alexander, 2014)](ea-principles-epistemics/isolated-demands-for-rigor.md) — Will Aldred ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/2fJXYmGLRRFDvyy9R/8-beware-isolated-demands-for-rigor-alexander-2014)) — Scott Alexander on selectively demanding rigor only for conclusions you dislike; an EA Handbook epistemics staple
- [Learning By Writing](ea-principles-epistemics/learning-by-writing.md) ([source](https://www.cold-takes.com/learning-by-writing/)) — Holden Karnofsky's method for developing real views on hard topics; becoming-Holden-like truth-seeking in practice
- [Minimal-trust investigations](ea-principles-epistemics/minimal-trust-investigations.md) ([source](https://www.cold-takes.com/minimal-trust-investigations/)) — Holden on checking a claim end-to-end yourself; the discipline behind deep truth-seeking
- [wolf1982.pdf](ea-principles-epistemics/moral-saints-wolf.md) ([source](https://r.jordan.im/download/philosophy/wolf1982.pdf)) — Susan Wolf's classic 'Moral Saints': a life maximally devoted to morality may not be admirable; the counterpoint every committed utilitarian should wrestle with ⚠️short
- [Naïve vs Prudent Utilitarianism](ea-principles-epistemics/naive-vs-prudent-utilitarianism.md) — Richard Y Chappell🔸 ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/nvus8kuGxyacyfXeg/naive-vs-prudent-utilitarianism)) — Chappell on why sophisticated utilitarians reject naive calculation; the reasoning virtue behind rule-of-thumb integrity
- [On caring](ea-principles-epistemics/on-caring.md) ([source](https://mindingourway.com/on-caring/)) — Nate Soares on scope insensitivity and caring by the numbers; the classic scope-sensitivity primer
- [Please Forgive the Errors in My Ways](ea-principles-epistemics/please-forgive.md) — alejoacelas ([source](https://myea.blog/please-forgive)) — Alejo's own essay on the virtue of openness/extreme honesty and its costs; his frontier-virtue seed for the collection
- [Book Review: The Scout Mindset](ea-principles-epistemics/scout-mindset-review.md) — Scott Alexander ([source](https://www.astralcodexten.com/p/book-review-the-scout-mindset)) — Scott Alexander's review of Galef's Scout Mindset; truth-seeking as soldier-vs-scout, top EA-recruiting book
- [Truthseeking is the ground in which other principles grow](ea-principles-epistemics/truthseeking-is-the-ground.md) — Elizabeth ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/XkLnbSsjK7TpNFgPn/truthseeking-is-the-ground-in-which-other-principles)) — Elizabeth argues truthseeking/contact-with-reality is the meta-principle underlying all consequentialist principles
- [Twelve Virtues of Rationality](ea-principles-epistemics/twelve-virtues-of-rationality.md) — Eliezer Yudkowsky ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/7ZqGiPHTpiDMwqMN2/twelve-virtues-of-rationality)) — Yudkowsky's canonical list of rationalist virtues; curiosity, relinquishment, humility, the way of the void
- [Useful Vices for Wicked Problems](ea-principles-epistemics/useful-vices-for-wicked-problems.md) ([source](https://www.cold-takes.com/useful-vices-for-wicked-problems/)) — Holden Karnofsky on laziness/impatience/hubris as antidotes to paralyzing conscientiousness on hard problems
- [Virtues for Real-World Utilitarians](ea-principles-epistemics/virtues-for-real-world-utilitarians.md) ([source](https://www.utilitarianism.net/guest-essays/virtues-for-real-world-utilitarians/)) — Schubert & Caviola on the six virtues real-world utilitarians should cultivate; the baseline-virtues piece Alejo wants to build past toward frontier virtues

The Better Futures series.](macaskill-worldview/flourishing-over-survival.md) — William_MacAskill ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/mzT2ZQGNce8AywAx3/should-we-aim-for-flourishing-over-mere-survival-the-better)) — MacAskill's Forum framing of surviving vs flourishing (Better Futures); the values strand of the worldview.

## macrostrategy (22)

- [Book Review: Age of Em](macrostrategy/age-of-em-review.md) ([source](https://slatestarcodex.com/2016/05/28/book-review-age-of-em/)) — Scott Alexander's review of Hanson's Age of Em; a rigorous alternative scenario (emulated minds, Malthusian competition) for how a post-AGI economy could unfold.
- [AI 2027](macrostrategy/ai-2027.md) ([source](https://ai-2027.com/)) — Kokotajlo et al.'s concrete month-by-month AGI scenario to 2027 and beyond; the current flagship strategy/scenario artifact an intro person should read.
- [AI Could Defeat All Of Us Combined](macrostrategy/ai-could-defeat-all-of-us.md) ([source](https://www.cold-takes.com/ai-could-defeat-all-of-us-combined/)) — Karnofsky's accessible case that misaligned AI could disempower humanity; a core scenario-layer reading connecting macrostrategy to AI risk.
- [All Possible Views About Humanity's Future Are Wild](macrostrategy/all-possible-views-are-wild.md) ([source](https://www.cold-takes.com/all-possible-views-about-humanitys-future-are-wild/)) — Karnofsky's argument that every coherent view of humanity's long-run future is 'wild'; trains the epistemic habit of taking strange-but-important conclusions seriously.
- [Astronomical Waste: The Opportunity Cost of Delayed Technological Development](macrostrategy/astronomical-waste.md) — Nick Bostrom ([source](https://nickbostrom.com/papers/astronomical-waste/)) — Bostrom's foundational argument that delaying safe space colonization carries astronomical opportunity cost; the scope-sensitivity classic underlying longtermist macrostrategy.
- [Book Review: Deep Utopia](macrostrategy/deep-utopia-review-acx.md) — Scott Alexander ([source](https://www.astralcodexten.com/p/book-review-deep-utopia)) — Scott Alexander's review of Bostrom's Deep Utopia; an accessible way to grapple with what a 'solved world' post-AGI could mean for meaning and value.
- [Digital People Would Be An Even Bigger Deal](macrostrategy/digital-people.md) ([source](https://www.cold-takes.com/how-digital-people-could-change-the-world/)) — Karnofsky on 'digital people' (whole-brain emulations): a concrete macrostrategy scenario for how the long-run future could be shaped and locked in.
- [Why despite global progress, humanity is probably facing its most dangerous time ever](macrostrategy/existential-risks-80k.md) ([source](https://80000hours.org/articles/existential-risks/)) — 80,000 Hours' problem profile on existential risk; a clean intro-level framing of why safeguarding humanity's long-term potential is a priority.
- [The Fable of the Dragon‑Tyrant](macrostrategy/fable-dragon-tyrant.md) — Nick Bostrom ([source](https://www.nickbostrom.com/fable/dragon.html)) — Bostrom's parable reframing aging/death as a defeatable dragon; an accessible on-ramp to why fighting existential threats and shaping the long-term future is a moral priority.
- [The Track Record of Futurists Seems ... Fine](macrostrategy/futurists-track-record.md) ([source](https://www.cold-takes.com/the-track-record-of-futurists-seems-fine/)) — Karnofsky examines whether long-range futurism has any track record; an epistemics reading for judging how much to trust big-picture forecasts.
- [Are we living at the most influential time in history?](macrostrategy/hinge-of-history-macaskill.md) — William_MacAskill ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/XXLf6FmWujkxna3E6/are-we-living-at-the-most-influential-time-in-history-1)) — MacAskill's argument that we are probably NOT at the most influential time in history; the anchor of the 'hinge of history' debate central to longtermist prioritization.
- [The Hinge of History Hypothesis: Reply to MacAskill (Andreas Mogensen)](macrostrategy/hinge-of-history-reply-mogensen.md) — Global Priorities Institute ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/idp4GEqWp24ocgfes/the-hinge-of-history-hypothesis-reply-to-macaskill-andreas)) — Mogensen's rebuttal to MacAskill on the hinge of history; supplies the counter-side of the debate so students see the argument contested.
- [Letter from Utopia](macrostrategy/letter-from-utopia.md) ([source](https://nickbostrom.com/utopia)) — Bostrom's 'Letter from Utopia': a short, vivid evocation of what a flourishing post-transition future could feel like; an emotional on-ramp to why shaping the far future matters.
- [Dario Amodei — Machines of Loving Grace](macrostrategy/machines-of-loving-grace.md) ([source](https://www.darioamodei.com/essay/machines-of-loving-grace)) — Amodei's optimistic big-picture vision of a post-AGI world; a frontier-lab-CEO counterpoint that gives intro readers a concrete 'better futures' target to reason about.
- [Meditations On Moloch](macrostrategy/meditations-on-moloch.md) ([source](https://slatestarcodex.com/2014/07/30/meditations-on-moloch/)) — Scott Alexander on Moloch: coordination failures and competitive dynamics that erode value; foundational for gradual-disempowerment and lock-in macrostrategy.
- [The 'most important century' blog post series](macrostrategy/most-important-century-roundup.md) ([source](https://www.cold-takes.com/most-important-century/)) — Karnofsky's roundup of the Most Important Century thesis; the best intro-level entry point to why this century may be the most pivotal in history.
- [Introduction - SITUATIONAL AWARENESS: The Decade Ahead](macrostrategy/situational-awareness.md) ([source](https://situational-awareness.ai/)) — Aschenbrenner's 'Situational Awareness': an influential (contestable) forecast of the decade to AGI/superintelligence and its geopolitical stakes.
- [How we could stumble into AI catastrophe](macrostrategy/stumble-into-ai-catastrophe.md) ([source](https://www.cold-takes.com/how-we-could-stumble-into-ai-catastrophe/)) — Karnofsky's concrete scenario of how a seemingly-normal path could stumble into AI catastrophe; bridges macrostrategy to actionable risk analysis.
- [Takeoff speeds](macrostrategy/takeoff-speeds-christiano.md) ([source](https://sideways-view.com/2018/02/24/takeoff-speeds/)) — Christiano's 'Takeoff speeds': slow vs fast intelligence-explosion dynamics; a key strategic variable shaping how much warning and steering room we get.
- [This Can't Go On](macrostrategy/this-cant-go-on.md) ([source](https://www.cold-takes.com/this-cant-go-on/)) — Karnofsky's economic-growth argument that current trends imply we live in an unusual, unsustainable period; a vivid intro to why transformative change may be near.
- [vulnerable.pdf](macrostrategy/vulnerable-world-hypothesis.md) ([source](https://nickbostrom.com/papers/vulnerable.pdf)) — Bostrom's Vulnerable World Hypothesis: if some future technology is a civilization-destroying 'black ball', avoiding catastrophe may require unprecedented preventive governance; core macrostrategy. ⚠️short
- [What failure looks like](macrostrategy/what-failure-looks-like.md) — paulfchristiano ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/HBxe6wdjxK239zajf/what-failure-looks-like)) — Christiano's canonical two-scenario picture of AI going wrong slowly ('going out with a whimper' / influence-seeking); a scenario-layer staple for intro readers.

- [Dario Amodei — Machines of Loving Grace](power-concentration-democracy/amodei-machines-of-loving-grace.md) ([source](https://darioamodei.com/essay/machines-of-loving-grace)) — Amodei on democracies keeping the upper hand on powerful AI; the 'entente' vision and its critics.
- [46 - Tom Davidson on AI-enabled Coups](power-concentration-democracy/axrp-tom-davidson-ai-enabled-coups.md) ([source](https://axrp.net/episode/2025/08/07/episode-46-tom-davidson-ai-enabled-coups.html)) — AXRP interview transcript with Davidson on AI-enabled coups; companion to the Forethought report.
- [Capital, AGI, and human ambition - Rudolf's Writing](power-concentration-democracy/capital-agi-and-human-ambition.md) ([source](https://rudolf.website/capital-agi-and-ambition/)) — L Rudolf L: labor-replacing AI makes capital a general substitute for humans, entrenching existing power; author's canonical version.
- [How to mitigate AI-driven power concentration - Future of Life Institute](power-concentration-democracy/fli-mitigate-power-concentration-rfp.md) ([source](https://futureoflife.org/grant-program/mitigate-ai-driven-power-concentration/)) — FLI grant RFP framing the problem and solution space; useful for curriculum design.
- [New Survey: Broad Expert Consensus for Many AGI Safety and Governance Practices | GovAI](power-concentration-democracy/govai-agi-governance-best-practices.md) ([source](https://www.governance.ai/analysis/broad-expert-consensus-for-many-agi-safety-and-governance-best-practices)) — GovAI survey: expert consensus on internal controls preventing any single actor from unilaterally deploying advanced AI.
- [Gradual Disempowerment: Systemic Existential Risks from Incremental AI Development](power-concentration-democracy/gradual-disempowerment-full.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/html/2501.16946v2)) — Full Kulveit et al paper: systemic existential risk from incremental AI eroding human influence over economy, culture, state.
- [AI and Leviathan: Part I](power-concentration-democracy/hammond-ai-and-leviathan-part-i.md) — Samuel Hammond ([source](https://www.secondbest.ca/p/ai-and-leviathan-part-i)) — Hammond: AI reshapes the state between despotic and absent Leviathan; institutional-disruption voice.
- [AI and Power Concentration: An Interview With Samuel Hammond](power-concentration-democracy/hammond-power-concentration-interview.md) — Power Concentration Newsletter ([source](https://powerconcentrationnewsletter.substack.com/p/ai-and-power-concentration-an-interview)) — Interview mapping the flavors and mechanisms of AI-driven power concentration.
- [The Intelligence Curse: an essay series](power-concentration-democracy/intelligence-curse-essay-series.md) — L Rudolf L ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/LCFgLY3EWb3Gqqxyi/the-intelligence-curse-an-essay-series)) — Drago & Laine: if AI removes powerful actors' need for ordinary people, states and firms stop caring for them; core power-concentration thesis.
- [The Intelligence Curse](power-concentration-democracy/intelligence-curse-original.md) — Luke Drago ([source](https://lukedrago.substack.com/p/the-intelligence-curse)) — Original Intelligence Curse essay; resource-curse analogy for an AGI economy.
- [Pyramid Replacement - The Intelligence Curse](power-concentration-democracy/intelligence-curse-pyramid-replacement.md) ([source](https://intelligence-curse.ai/pyramid/)) — Pyramid replacement: AI hollows out corporate ladders bottom-up, freezing social mobility.
- [Lock-In Threat Models](power-concentration-democracy/lock-in-threat-models.md) — Alfie Lamerton ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/gmFadztDHePBz7SRm/lock-in-threat-models)) — Threat models for how value/power lock-in could concretely happen.
- [Sense-making about extreme power concentration](power-concentration-democracy/sense-making-extreme-power-concentration.md) — rosehadshar ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/tnkEoTxdGCsBFRQty/sense-making-about-extreme-power-concentration)) — Structured breakdown of what drives extreme power concentration risk; checks-and-balances framing.
- [Stable totalitarianism: an overview](power-concentration-democracy/stable-totalitarianism-an-overview.md) — 80000_Hours ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/Ljae6jJEwifD3QCr2/stable-totalitarianism-an-overview)) — EA Forum overview of stable-totalitarianism mechanisms and probability.
- [d/acc: one year later](power-concentration-democracy/vitalik-dacc-one-year-later.md) ([source](https://vitalik.eth.limo/general/2025/01/05/dacc2.html)) — Buterin's d/acc: decentralized, defensive tech as an alternative to centralizing power in one authority.
- [#194 –  Defensive acceleration and how to regulate AI when you fear government (Vitalik Buterin on the 80,000 Hours Podcast)](power-concentration-democracy/vitalik-defensive-acceleration-transcript.md) — 80000_Hours ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/tc7z9tA55i2ScZS7Z/194-defensive-acceleration-and-how-to-regulate-ai-when-you)) — Vitalik on 80k (forum transcript): regulating AI when you fear government capture; distributive alternative to concentration.
- [What is Lock-In?](power-concentration-democracy/what-is-lock-in.md) — Alfie Lamerton ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/F4ji5dvvCk8tBAsXw/what-is-lock-in)) — Conceptual primer on lock-in, the mechanism underlying durable power concentration.
- [Cullen O'Keefe: The Windfall Clause — Sharing the Benefits of Advanced AI | Effective Altruism](power-concentration-democracy/windfall-clause.md) ([source](https://www.effectivealtruism.org/articles/cullen-okeefe-the-windfall-clause-sharing-the-benefits-of-advanced-ai)) — O'Keefe/GovAI proposal to pre-commit AI firms to share windfall profits; a concrete anti-concentration mechanism.

## richard-ngo (21)

- [21st Century Civilization curriculum](richard-ngo/21st-century-civilization-curriculum.md) — Richard Ngo ([source](https://www.mindthefuture.info/p/21st-century-civilization-curriculum)) — Ngo's own proposed curriculum for the age of AGI; a direct model/competitor for what this fellowship is trying to build.
- [Agents as webs of beliefs](richard-ngo/agents-as-webs-of-beliefs.md) — Richard Ngo ([source](https://www.mindthefuture.info/p/agents-as-webs-of-beliefs)) — Recent Ngo essay modeling agents as belief-webs; extends his scale-free agency and epistemology program.
- [AGI safety career advice](richard-ngo/agi-safety-career-advice.md) — Richard_Ngo ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/ho63vCb2MNFijinzY/agi-safety-career-advice)) — His most-cited career guidance: find a big lever, choose your role by personal fit; a template for AGI-era career thinking.
- [AGI safety from first principles: Introduction](richard-ngo/agi-safety-from-first-principles.md) — Richard_Ngo ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/8xRSjC76HasLnMGSf/agi-safety-from-first-principles-introduction)) — Ngo's foundational reframing of why AGI could pose x-risk, built up from deep-learning first principles rather than legacy arguments.
- [Twitter thread on AI takeover scenarios](richard-ngo/ai-takeover-scenarios.md) — Richard_Ngo ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/tPfqnropv3WfchhYB/twitter-thread-on-ai-takeover-scenarios)) — Ngo's accessible sketch of how AI takeover could concretely unfold; useful narrative bridge for newcomers.
- [Aligning to Virtues](richard-ngo/aligning-to-virtues.md) — Richard Ngo ([source](https://www.mindthefuture.info/p/aligning-to-virtues)) — Ngo's case for training AI (and people) toward virtues rather than rules; directly relevant to MacAskill's AI-character cause area.
- [The Alignment Problem from a Deep Learning Perspective  (major rewrite)](richard-ngo/alignment-problem-deep-learning-perspective.md) — SoerenMind ([source](https://www.alignmentforum.org/posts/5GxLiJJEzvqmTNyCK/the-alignment-problem-from-a-deep-learning-perspective-major)) — The canonical technical statement of the misalignment case (deception, misgeneralized goals, power-seeking) grounded in ML.
- [Clarifying and predicting AGI](richard-ngo/clarifying-and-predicting-agi.md) — Richard_Ngo ([source](https://www.alignmentforum.org/posts/BoA3agdkAzL6HQtQP/clarifying-and-predicting-agi)) — Ngo's t-AGI framework: replaces a single AGI threshold with 1-minute/1-hour/1-day capability horizons for forecasting.
- [Some cruxes on impactful alternatives to AI policy work](richard-ngo/cruxes-alternatives-to-ai-policy-work.md) — richard_ngo ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/DW4FyzRTfBfNDWm6J/some-cruxes-on-impactful-alternatives-to-ai-policy-work)) — Early Ngo dialogue mapping cruxes on how to have impact beyond AI policy; models his cause-prioritization style.
- [Distributed vs centralized agents](richard-ngo/distributed-vs-centralized-agents.md) — Richard Ngo ([source](https://www.mindthefuture.info/p/distributed-vs-centralized-agents)) — Introduces coalitional agency by contrasting distributed and centralized control; foundational to his agency theory.
- [Economic efficiency often undermines sociopolitical autonomy](richard-ngo/economic-efficiency-undermines-autonomy.md) — Richard Ngo ([source](https://www.mindthefuture.info/p/economic-efficiency-often-undermines)) — Argues efficiency can erode sociopolitical autonomy; a worldview piece on gradual-disempowerment-adjacent dynamics.
- [Elite Coordination via the Consensus of Power](richard-ngo/elite-coordination-consensus-of-power.md) — Richard Ngo ([source](https://www.mindthefuture.info/p/elite-coordination-via-the-consensus)) — How elites coordinate via perceived consensus of power; his political-economy lens on legitimacy and coups.
- [Lessons from my time in Effective Altruism](richard-ngo/lessons-from-my-time-in-ea.md) — richard_ngo ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/ctnMCdTH7dmiN4jBx/lessons-from-my-time-in-effective-altruism)) — Ngo's personal reflection on EA: what the movement got right and wrong, from an insider turned critic.
- [Meditations on Mot](richard-ngo/meditations-on-mot.md) — Richard Ngo ([source](https://www.mindthefuture.info/p/meditations-on-mot)) — Ngo on Moloch/egregores and coordination failure; a worldview piece on the forces that shape civilizational outcomes.
- [On Pessimization](richard-ngo/on-pessimization.md) — Richard Ngo ([source](https://www.mindthefuture.info/p/on-pessimization)) — Why coalitions nominally devoted to a goal can actively work against it; a lens on institutional and movement failure modes.
- [Power Lies Trembling](richard-ngo/power-lies-trembling.md) — Richard Ngo ([source](https://www.mindthefuture.info/p/power-lies-trembling)) — On revolt, legitimacy, and what makes a well-governed coalition; governance-as-coalitional-agency applied to politics.
- [Realism about rationality](richard-ngo/realism-about-rationality.md) — Richard_Ngo ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/suxvE2ddnYMPJN9HD/realism-about-rationality)) — Classic Ngo epistemics essay: dissects the assumption that there's one correct theory of intelligence/rationality.
- [Towards a scale-free theory of intelligent agency](richard-ngo/scale-free-theory-of-intelligent-agency.md) — Richard Ngo ([source](https://www.mindthefuture.info/p/towards-a-scale-free-theory-of-intelligent)) — Ngo's coalitional-agency thesis: agents as competing/cooperating subagents at every scale; his core framework for minds and societies.
- [The Gentle Romance](richard-ngo/the-gentle-romance-fiction.md) — Richard Ngo ([source](https://www.asimov.press/p/gentle-romance)) — Ngo's flagship short story on living through the transition to utopia; his fiction as a mode of AGI worldview-building.
- [Towards a Formal Scientific Epistemology](richard-ngo/towards-a-formal-scientific-epistemology.md) — Richard Ngo ([source](https://www.mindthefuture.info/p/towards-a-formal-scientific-epistemology)) — Ngo's attempt at a formal epistemology; the values-and-epistemic-habits thread MacAskill says the curriculum needs.
- [Well-foundedness as an organizing principle of healthy minds and societies](richard-ngo/well-foundedness.md) — Richard Ngo ([source](https://www.mindthefuture.info/p/well-foundedness-as-an-organizing)) — Organizing principle for healthy minds and societies: conflicts between subagents shouldn't propagate downward.

## s-risks (23)

- [‘S-risks’ | 80,000 Hours](s-risks/80k-s-risks-problem-profile.md) ([source](https://80000hours.org/problem-profiles/s-risks/)) — 80,000 Hours problem profile: the mainstream-EA framing of s-risks, ideal bridge reading for a fellowship.
- [Astronomical suffering from slightly misaligned artificial intelligence](s-risks/astronomical-suffering-slightly-misaligned-ai.md) ([source](https://reducing-suffering.org/near-miss/)) — Tomasik on how near-miss (slightly misaligned) AI could be worse than total misalignment; the sharpest s-risk-from-AI argument.
- [Avoiding the Worst: How to Prevent a Moral Catastrophe](s-risks/avoiding-the-worst-book.md) ([source](https://centerforreducingsuffering.org/research/avoiding-the-worst/)) — Landing page for Baumann's book Avoiding the Worst, the first comprehensive s-risk introduction; anchor deeper reading.
- [Beginner’s guide to reducing s-risks – Center on Long-Term Risk](s-risks/beginners-guide-to-reducing-s-risks.md) — Anthony DiGiovanni ([source](https://longtermrisk.org/beginners-guide-to-reducing-s-risks/)) — CLR's beginner on-ramp: what s-risks are and concrete ways to reduce them; accessible core reading.
- [Priority areas (Archive) – Center on Long-Term Risk](s-risks/clr-priority-areas.md) ([source](https://longtermrisk.org/priority-areas/)) — CLR's current priority areas; shows where the leading s-risk org actually focuses its work today.
- [CLR's recent work on multi-agent systems](s-risks/clr-recent-work-multi-agent-systems.md) — JesseClifton ([source](https://www.alignmentforum.org/posts/EzoCZjTdWTMgacKGS/clr-s-recent-work-on-multi-agent-systems)) — CLR's own overview of its multi-agent research program; shows what cooperative-AI s-risk work looks like in practice.
- [Cooperation, Conflict, and Transformative Artificial Intelligence: A Research Agenda – Center on Long-Term Risk](s-risks/cooperation-conflict-tai-research-agenda.md) ([source](https://longtermrisk.org/research-agenda/)) — CLR's Cooperation, Conflict & TAI research agenda; the load-bearing statement of cooperative-AI-as-s-risk-reduction.
- [Coordination challenges for preventing AI conflict – Center on Long-Term Risk](s-risks/coordination-challenges-preventing-ai-conflict.md) — Stefan Torges ([source](https://longtermrisk.org/coordination-challenges-for-preventing-ai-conflict/)) — CLR on how AI conflict could cause suffering and why coordination is hard; concrete cooperative-AI s-risk pathway.
- [EA reading list: suffering-focused ethics](s-risks/ea-reading-list-suffering-focused-ethics.md) — richard_ngo ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/vTr2SBpkszjwzXLQT/ea-reading-list-suffering-focused-ethics)) — Curated suffering-focused-ethics reading list; useful for curriculum design and finding further sources.
- [How can we reduce s-risks?](s-risks/how-can-we-reduce-s-risks.md) ([source](https://centerforreducingsuffering.org/research/how-can-we-reduce-s-risks/)) — CRS survey of concrete interventions to reduce s-risks; the tractability half of the case.
- [Introduction to suffering-focused ethics](s-risks/introduction-to-suffering-focused-ethics.md) — Center for Reducing Suffering ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/wLEyoncFCmDyqPA5f/introduction-to-suffering-focused-ethics-1)) — Vinding's intro to suffering-focused ethics, the value theory underpinning s-risk priority; core for the values strand.
- [Reasons for optimism about measuring malevolence to tackle x- and s-risks](s-risks/measuring-malevolence-x-and-s-risks.md) — Jamie_Harris ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/SFkRrs2BCa5ieeMej/reasons-for-optimism-about-measuring-malevolence-to-tackle-x)) — Recent follow-up on operationalizing malevolence measurement; a concrete, tractable s-risk research direction.
- [New Report: Multi-Agent Risks from Advanced AI](s-risks/multi-agent-risks-from-advanced-ai.md) ([source](https://www.cooperativeai.com/post/new-report-multi-agent-risks-from-advanced-ai)) — Cooperative AI Foundation report (50+ researchers) mapping multi-agent risks; bridges s-risk concerns to mainstream AI safety.
- [Reducing long-term risks from malevolent actors](s-risks/reducing-long-term-risks-from-malevolent-actors.md) — David_Althaus ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/LpkXtFXdsRd4rG8Kb/reducing-long-term-risks-from-malevolent-actors)) — Althaus & Baumann on malevolence as a cross-cutting s-risk factor; concrete, tractable, links s-risks to power concentration.
- [Reducing Risks of Astronomical Suffering: A Neglected Priority – Center on Long-Term Risk](s-risks/reducing-risks-astronomical-suffering-neglected-priority.md) — David Althaus, Lukas Gloor ([source](https://longtermrisk.org/reducing-risks-of-astronomical-suffering-a-neglected-priority/)) — Althaus & Gloor foundational paper introducing the s-risk vs x-risk distinction; load-bearing deeper reading.
- [Risk factors for s-risks](s-risks/risk-factors-for-s-risks.md) ([source](https://centerforreducingsuffering.org/research/risk-factors-for-s-risks/)) — The risk-factors framing: which conditions (conflict, malevolence, value differences) make s-risks likelier; core to the CLR/CRS worldview.
- [Risks of Astronomical Future Suffering – Center on Long-Term Risk](s-risks/risks-of-astronomical-future-suffering.md) — Brian Tomasik ([source](https://longtermrisk.org/risks-of-astronomical-future-suffering/)) — Tomasik's foundational 2011 essay; the origin of the astronomical-suffering framing that seeded the whole field.
- [S-risk FAQ – Center on Long-Term Risk](s-risks/s-risk-faq.md) — Tobias Baumann ([source](https://longtermrisk.org/s-risk-faq/)) — CLR's FAQ answering common objections and confusions; useful discussion-prompt material for a fellowship.
- [S-risks: An introduction](s-risks/s-risks-an-introduction.md) ([source](https://centerforreducingsuffering.org/research/intro/)) — Baumann's canonical short intro to s-risks; strongest candidate for a core intro-fellowship reading on the lens.
- [S-Risks: Fates Worse Than Extinction](s-risks/s-risks-fates-worse-than-extinction.md) — aggliu ([source](https://www.lesswrong.com/posts/bDoGbZX7Jzjr2x3Aa/s-risks-fates-worse-than-extinction)) — Accessible LessWrong explainer of s-risks; a gentle, well-written on-ramp for newcomers.
- [S-risks: Why they are the worst existential risks, and how to prevent them (EAG Boston 2017) – Center on Long-Term Risk](s-risks/s-risks-why-worst-existential-risks-eag-2017.md) — Max Daniel ([source](https://longtermrisk.org/s-risks-talk-eag-boston-2017/)) — Baumann's classic 2017 EAG talk transcript; the movement-defining pitch for s-risks as worst-case x-risks.
- [Solving alignment isn't enough for a flourishing future](s-risks/solving-alignment-isnt-enough.md) ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/oEpGBqDCo2z5pbpvA/solving-alignment-isn-t-enough-for-a-flourishing-future)) — Argues alignment success doesn't guarantee a good future; frames s-risks/quality-of-future as distinct from extinction. Strong core-reading candidate.
- [Suffering-Focused Ethics: Defense and Implications](s-risks/suffering-focused-ethics-defense-and-implications.md) ([source](https://magnusvinding.com/2020/05/31/suffering-focused-ethics-defense-and-implications/)) — Landing page for Vinding's book-length defense of suffering-focused ethics; the deeper theoretical anchor for the values strand.

## space-governance (21)

- [Announcing the Center for Space Governance](space-governance/announcing-center-for-space-governance.md) — Space Governance ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/5HEFJKHGpcT49RK6y/announcing-the-center-for-space-governance)) — Founding of the Center for Space Governance — the field-building institution in this lens.
- [Announcing the Space Futures Initiative](space-governance/announcing-space-futures-initiative.md) ([source](https://ea.greaterwrong.com/posts/x5czbdCW6SqnLJhbD/announcing-the-space-futures-initiative)) — Space Futures Initiative launch — student/research pipeline for longtermist space governance.
- [Spamming%20the%20universe.pdf](space-governance/armstrong-sandberg-eternity-in-six-hours.md) ([source](https://www.aleph.se/papers/Spamming%20the%20universe.pdf)) — Armstrong & Sandberg show intergalactic colonization is technically feasible — the feasibility premise behind space longtermism. ⚠️short
- [Nick Beckstead - A conversation with Charlie Stross on Space Colonization on 30 April 2014](space-governance/beckstead-stross-space-colonization.md) ([source](https://www.nickbeckstead.com/conversations/stross)) — Beckstead's conversation with sci-fi author Charles Stross — a skeptic's economics of interstellar settlement.
- [Astronomical Waste: The Opportunity Cost of Delayed Technological Development](space-governance/bostrom-astronomical-waste.md) — Nick Bostrom ([source](https://nickbostrom.com/papers/astronomical-waste/)) — Bostrom's foundational argument: the cosmic endowment and the opportunity cost of delayed colonization — why the future's scale is the core stake in space.
- [Summary of and thoughts on 'Dark Skies' by Daniel Deudney](space-governance/dark-skies-deudney-summary.md) — Cody_Fenwick ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/YKqKv8tckMHkmFB4z/summary-of-and-thoughts-on-dark-skies-by-daniel-deudney)) — EA Forum summary of Deudney's Dark Skies — the strongest anti-space-expansion case, that settlement raises existential and totalitarian risk.
- [Will we eventually be able to colonize other stars? Notes from a preliminary review](space-governance/fhi-colonize-other-stars.md) — Nick_Beckstead ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/5dgFWods87kkE9TpZ/will-we-eventually-be-able-to-colonize-other-stars-notes)) — FHI review of the feasibility of interstellar colonization — grounds the whole cause in physics and engineering.
- [How to Make the Future Better: Concrete Actions for Flourishing](space-governance/forethought-how-to-make-the-future-better.md) ([source](https://www.forethought.org/research/how-to-make-the-future-better)) — MacAskill's Better Futures capstone (cited in the source essay) — space settlement as a mechanism for long-lasting cosmic lock-in.
- [filluniv.pdf](space-governance/hanson-burning-the-cosmic-commons.md) ([source](https://mason.gmu.edu/~rhanson/filluniv.pdf)) — Robin Hanson's evolutionary model of interstellar colonization — competitive expansion 'burns' cosmic resources, a warning about ungoverned space races. ⚠️short
- [Influencing United Nations Space Governance](space-governance/influencing-un-space-governance.md) ([source](https://ea.greaterwrong.com/posts/x7ynaoXWSy7FQANio/influencing-united-nations-space-governance)) — Concrete policy path: influencing UN space governance processes — the tractable end of the cause.
- [An Informal Review of Space Exploration](space-governance/informal-review-of-space-exploration.md) — kbog ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/xxcroGWRieSQjCw2N/an-informal-review-of-space-exploration)) — Skeptical informal review weighing space exploration's value from an EA lens.
- [Space governance - Problem profile](space-governance/moorhouse-80k-space-governance-profile.md) ([source](https://80000hours.org/problem-profiles/space-governance/)) — Fin Moorhouse's 80,000 Hours problem profile — the canonical EA case for space governance as a pressing, potentially top-priority problem.
- [2209.06186](space-governance/nutshell-kings-space-settlement-controversial.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/pdf/2209.06186)) — Torres/Baum-style analysis of why human space settlement is controversial — maps the ethical fault lines for classroom debate. ⚠️short
- [2104.01191](space-governance/ord-edges-of-our-universe.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/pdf/2104.01191)) — Toby Ord maps the affectable universe — the physical bounds on what a spacefaring civilization could ever reach. ⚠️short
- [1608.01989](space-governance/peaks-of-eternal-light-moon-property.md) ([source](https://arxiv.org/pdf/1608.01989)) — The Peaks of Eternal Light: a concrete near-term lunar property-rights problem where space governance decisions get locked in early. ⚠️short
- [Why don’t we see alien civilizations? This Oxford academic suspects they're sleeping. Here’s the reason.](space-governance/sandberg-80k-fermi-paradox.md) — Anders Sandberg (80,000 Hours Podcast) ([source](https://80000hours.org/podcast/episodes/anders-sandberg-fermi-paradox/)) — Anders Sandberg 80k interview (full transcript) — Fermi paradox resolutions and how a civilization could colonize the universe.
- [Anders Sandberg on war in space, whether civilisations age, and the best things possible in our universe | 80,000 Hours](space-governance/sandberg-80k-war-in-space-best-things.md) — Anders Sandberg (80,000 Hours Podcast) ([source](https://80000hours.org/podcast/episodes/anders-sandberg-best-things-possible-in-our-universe/)) — Anders Sandberg 80k interview (full transcript) — war in space, defense-dominance, and the best futures physically possible in our universe.
- [Spreading happiness to the stars seems little harder than just spreading](space-governance/shulman-spreading-happiness-to-stars.md) ([source](http://reflectivedisequilibrium.blogspot.com/2012/09/spreading-happiness-to-stars-seems.html)) — Carl Shulman argues spreading welfare across the stars is barely harder than spreading — bears on whether a space future is good, not just big.
- [Space governance is important, tractable and neglected](space-governance/space-governance-important-tractable-neglected.md) — Tobias_Baumann ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/QkRq6aRA84vv4xsu9/space-governance-is-important-tractable-and-neglected)) — ITN framing of space governance as an EA cause area.
- [Space Governance is not a cause area](space-governance/space-governance-is-not-a-cause-area.md) — JordanStone ([source](https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/posts/6kwbebYw2eHKCqyCL/space-governance-is-not-a-cause-area)) — Counterpoint: argues space governance is a meta/cross-cutting area rather than a standalone cause — sharpens the debate.
- [Conceptual models of space colonization - Charlie's Diary](space-governance/stross-conceptual-models-space-colonization.md) ([source](https://www.antipope.org/charlie/blog-static/2024/10/conceptual-models-of-space-col.html)) — Charles Stross's 2024 taxonomy of space-colonization models — an outside, skeptical voice on why settlement narratives mislead.
